vales: the instance store that should be used for writing alert instances,\n   485→// and an alert instance reader that can be used to read alert instances on startup.\n   486→func initInstanceStore(sqlStore db.DB, logger log.Logger, featureToggles featuremgmt.FeatureToggles) (state.InstanceStore, state.InstanceReader) {\n   487→\tvar instanceStore state.InstanceStore\n   488→\n   489→\t// We init both stores here, but only one will be used based on the feature toggles.\n   490→\t// Two stores are needed for the multi-instance reader to work correctly.\n   491→\t// It's used to read the state of alerts on startup, and allows switching the feature\n   492→\t// flags seamlessly without losing the state of alerts.\n   493→\tprotoInstanceStore := store.ProtoInstanceDBStore{\n   494→\t\tSQLStore:       sqlStore,\n   495→\t\tLogger:         logger,\n   496→\t\tFeatureToggles: featureToggles,\n   497→\t}\n   498→\tsimpleInstanceStore := store.InstanceDBStore{\n   499→\t\tSQLStore: sqlStore,\n   500→\t\tLogger:   logger,\n   501→\t}\n   502→\n   503→\tif featureToggles.IsEnabledGlobally(featuremgmt.FlagAlertingSaveStateCompressed) {\n   504→\t\tlogger.Info(\"Using protobuf-based alert instance store\")\n   505→\t\tinstanceStore = protoInstanceStore\n   506→\t\t// If FlagAlertingSaveStateCompressed is enabled, ProtoInstanceDBStore is used,\n   507→\t\t// which functions differently from InstanceDBStore. FlagAlertingSaveStatePeriodic is\n   508→\t\t// not applicable to ProtoInstanceDBStore, so a warning is logged if it is set.\n   509→\t\tif featureToggles.IsEnabledGlobally(featuremgmt.FlagAlertingSaveStatePeriodic) {\n   510→\t\t\tlogger.Warn(\"alertingSaveStatePeriodic is not used when alertingSaveStateCompressed feature flag enabled\")\n   511→\t\t}\n   512→\t} else {\n   513→\t\tlogger.Info(\"Using simple database alert instance store\")\n   514→\t\tinstanceStore = simpleInstanceStore\n   515→\t}\n   516→\n   517→\treturn instanceStore, state.NewMultiInstanceReader(logger, protoInstanceStore, simpleInstanceStore)\n   518→}\n   519→\n   520→func initStatePersister(uaCfg setting.UnifiedAlertingSettings, cfg state.ManagerCfg, featureToggles featuremgmt.FeatureToggles) state.StatePersister {\n   521→\tlogger := log.New(\"ngalert.state.manager.persist\")\n   522→\tvar statePersister state.StatePersister\n   523→\n   524→\tif featureToggles.IsEnabledGlobally(featuremgmt.FlagAlertingSaveStateCompressed) {\n   525→\t\tlogger.Info(\"Using rule state persister\")\n   526→\t\tstatePersister = 539→func subscribeToFolderChanges(logger log.Logger, bus bus.Bus, dbStore api.RuleStore) {\n   540→\t// if full path to the folder is changed, we update all alert rules in that folder to make sure that all peers (in HA mode) will update folder title and\n   541→\t// clean up the current state\n   542→\tbus.AddEventListener(func(ctx context.Context, evt *events.FolderFullPathUpdated) error {\n   543→\t\tlogger.Info(\"Got folder full path updated event. updating rules in the folders\", \"folderUIDs\", evt.UIDs)\n   544→\t\tupdatedKeys, err := dbStore.IncreaseVersionForAllRulesInNamespaces(ctx, evt.OrgID, evt.UIDs)\n   545→\t\tif err != nil {\n   546→\t\t\tlogger.Error(\"Failed to update alert rules in the folders after their full paths were changed\", \"error\", err, \"folderUIDs\", evt.UIDs, \"orgID\", evt.OrgID)\n   547→\t\t\treturn err\n   548→\t\t}\n   549→\t\tlogger.Info(\"Updated version for alert rules\", \"keys\", updatedKeys)\n   550→\t\treturn nil\n   551→\t})\n   552→}\n   553→\n   554→// Run starts the scheduler and Alertmanager.\n   555→func (ng *AlertNG) Run(ctx context.Context) error {\n   556→\tng.Log.Debug(\"Starting\", \"execute_alerts\", ng.Cfg.UnifiedAlerting.ExecuteAlerts)\n   557→\n   558→\tchildren, subCtx := errgroup.WithContext(ctx)\n   559→\n   560→\tchildren.Go(func() error {\n   561→\t\treturn ng.MultiOrgAlertmanager.Run(subCtx)\n   562→\t})\n   563→\tchildren.Go(func() error {\n   564→\t\treturn ng.AlertsRouter.Run(subCtx)\n   565→\t})\n   566→\n   567→\tif ng.Cfg.UnifiedAlerting.ExecuteAlerts {\n   568→\t\t// Only Warm() the state manager if we are actually executing alerts.\n   569→\t\t// Doing so when we are not executing alerts is wasteful and could lead\n   570→\t\t// to misleading rule status queries, as the status returned will be\n   571→\t\t// always based on the state loaded from the database at startup, and\n   572→\t\t// not the most recent evaluation state.\n   573→\t\t//\n   574→\t\t// Also note that this runs synchronously to ensure state is loaded\n   575→\t\t// before rule evaluation begins, hence we use ctx and not subCtx.\n   576→\t\t//\n   577→\t\tng.stateManager.Warm(ctx, ng.store, ng.store, ng.StartupInstanceReader)\n   578→\n   579→\t\tchildren.Go(func() error {\n   580→\t\t\treturn ng.schedule.Run(subCtx)\n   581→\t\t})\n   582→\t\tchildren.Go(func() error {\n   583→\t\t\treturn ng.stateManager.Run(subCtx)\n   584→\t\t})\n   585→\t}\n   586→\treturn children.Wait()\n   587→}\n   588→\n   589→// IsDisabled returns true if the alerting service is disabled for this instance.\n   590→func (ng *AlertNG) IsDisabled() bool {\n   591→\tif ng.Cfg == nil {\n   592→\t\treturn true\n   593→\t}\n   594→\n   595→\treturn !ng.Cfg.UnifiedAlerting.IsEnabled()\n   596→}\n   597→\n   598→// GetHooks returns a facility for replacing handlers for paths. The handler hook for a path\n   599→// is invoked after all other middleware is invoked (authentication, instrumentation).\n   600→func (ng *AlertNG) GetHooks() *api.Hooks {\n   601→\treturn ng.Api.Hooks\n   602→}\n   603→\n   604→type Historian interface {\n   605→\tapi.Historian\n   606→\tstate.Historian\n   607→}\n   608→\n   609→func configureHistorianBackend(\n   610→\tctx context.Context,\n   611→\tcfg setting.UnifiedAlertingStateHistorySettings,\n   612→\tar annotations.Repository,\n   613→\tds dashboards.DashboardService,\n   614→\trs historian.RuleStore,\n   615→\tmet *metrics.Historian,\n   616→\tl log.Logger,\n   617→\ttracer tracing.Tracer,\n   618→\tac historian.AccessControl,\n   619→\tdatasourceService datasources.DataSourceService,\n   620→\thttpClientProvider httpclient.Provider,\n   621→\tpluginContextProvider *plugincontext.Provider,\n   622→\tclock clock.Clock,\n   623→\tmw *metrics.RemoteWriter,\n   624→) (Historian, error) {\n   625→\tif !cfg.Enabled {\n   626→\t\tmet.Info.WithLabelValues(\"noop\").Set(0)\n   627→\t\treturn historian.NewNopHistorian(), nil\n   628→\t}\n   629→\n   630→\tbackend, err := historian.ParseBackendType(cfg.Backend)\n   631→\tif err != nil {\n   632→\t\treturn nil, err\n   633→\t}\n   634→\n   635→\tmet.Info.WithLabelValues(backend.String()).Set(1)\n   636→\tif backend == historian.BackendTypeMultiple {\n   637→\t\tprimaryCfg := cfg\n   638→\t\tprimaryCfg.Backend = cfg.MultiPrimary\n   639→\t\tprimary, err := configureHistorianBackend(ctx, primaryCfg, ar, ds, rs, met, l, tracer, ac, datasourceService, httpClientProvider, pluginContextProvider, clock, mw)\n   640→\t\tif err != nil {\n   641→\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"multi-backend target \\\"%s\\\" was misconfigured: %w\", cfg.MultiPrimary, err)\n   642→\t\t}\n   643→\n   644→\t\tvar secondaries []historian.Backend\n   645→\t\tfor _, b := range cfg.MultiSecondaries {\n   646→\t\t\tsecCfg := cfg\n   647→\t\t\tsecCfg.Backend = b\n   648→\t\t\tsec, err := configureHistorianBackend(ctx, secCfg, ar, ds, rs, met, l, tracer, ac, datasourceService, httpClientProvider, pluginContextProvider, clock, mw)\n   649→\t\t\tif err != nil {\n   650→\t\t\t\treturn nil, fmt.Errorf(\"multi-backend target \\\"%s\\\" was miconfigured: %w\", b, err)\n   651→\t\t\t}\n   652→\t\t\tsecondaries = append(secondaries, sec)\n   653→\t\t}\n   654→\n   655→\t\tl.Info(\"State history is operating in multi-backend mode\", \"primary\", cfg.MultiPrimary, \"secondaries\", cfg.MultiSecondaries)\n   656→\t\treturn historian.NewMultipleBackend(primary, secondaries...), nil\n   657→\t}\n   658→\tif backend == historian.BackendTypeAnnotations {\n   659→\t\tstore := historian.NewAnnotationStore(ar, ds, met)\n   660→\t\tlogCtx := log.WithContextualAttributes(ctx, []any{\"backend\", \"annotations\"})\n   661→\t\tannotationBackendLogger := log.New(\"ngalert.state.historian\").FromContext(logCtx)\n \"The Grafana unified alerting (ngalert) subsystem is composed of five major interconnected components, orchestrated through the AlertNG service (pkg/services/ngalert/ngalert.go). Here is how they interact:\\n\\n**1. Alert Rule Storage (Store Package)**\\nThe DBstore (pkg/services/ngalert/store/database.go) is the central data layer managing all alert rule definitions in the database. It implements the AlertingStore interface and coordinates with:\\n- alert_rule.go: Handles CRUD operations for alert rules\\n- instance_database.go and proto_instance_database.go: Store alert instance states with two implementations—one for simple JSON storage and one for compressed protobuf format\\n- alertmanager.go: Stores alertmanager configuration\\n- deltas.go and models.go: Manages rule changes and data structures\\n\\n**2. Scheduler (Schedule Package)**\\nThe schedule.go file implements the ScheduleService interface and is the execution engine that evaluates alert rules. Key components:\\n- NewScheduler() creates the scheduler with a RulesStore dependency\\n- alert_rule.go: Executes individual alert rules by querying data sources\\n- recording_rule.go: Executes Prometheus recording rules\\n- registry.go: Maintains a registry of all active rules and their evaluation state\\n- ticker/ticker.go: Manages evaluation intervals and timing\\n- retry.go: Implements backoff strategy for failed evaluations\\nThe scheduler fetches rules from DBstore.GetAlertRulesForScheduling() and evaluates them using the EvaluatorFactory.\\n\\n**3. State Manager (State Package)**\\nThe Manager (pkg/services/ngalert/state/manager.go) tracks the lifecycle of alert instances:\\n- manager.go: Core state tracking with NewManager() initialization\\n- state.go: State transition definitions (Normal, Alerting, Pending, NoData)\\n- cache.go: In-memory state cache for efficient lookups\\n- persist.go: StatePersister interface with three implementations:\\n  - persister_sync.go: Synchronous persistence\\n  - persister_async.go: Asynchronous periodic persistence\\n  - persister_sync_rule.go: Rule-aware state persistence\\n- multi_instance_reader.go: Handles state loading from database during startup\\nAfter the scheduler evaluates a rule, it sends state transitions to the state manager, which persists them to the instance database and forwards them to the notifier.\\n\\n**4. Notifier (Notifier Package)**\\nThe notification system manages alert routing to external systems:\\n- multiorg_alertmanager.go: MultiOrgAlertmanager orchestrates Alertmanager instances per organization\\n- alertmanager.go: Individual Alertmanager implementation wrapping the upstream Prometheus Alertmanager\\n- receiver_svc.go: ReceiverService manages contact point configurations\\n- silence_svc.go: SilenceService manages silences and mute timings\\n- alertmanager_config.go and config.go: Handle configuration persistence and validation\\n- alerts.go and silences.go: State management for alerts and silences\\nThe sender/router.go (AlertsRouter) sends state transitions from the state manager to the appropriate Alertmanager instance, which applies routing and grouping rules before sending to external notification channels.\\n\\n**5. History Writer (State/Historian Package)**\\nThe historian subsystem records alert state transitions for audit and querying:\\n- core.go: Core historian logic determining which transitions to record\\n- backend.go: Backend interface for pluggable storage\\n- Multiple backend implementations:\\n  - annotation.go: Stores state in Grafana annotations (AnnotationBackend)\\n  - loki.go: Remote Loki instance (RemoteLokiBackend)\\n  - prometheus.go: Prometheus remote write (RemotePrometheusBackend)\\n  - multiple.go: MultipleBackend for concurrent writes\\n- query.go: Queries historical state data\\n- model/rule.go: Historical rule models\\nThe state manager calls historian.Record() for each state transition, persisting them to the configured backend(s) for historical querying via the API.\\n\\n**Supporting Components:**\\n- eval/eval.go: Evaluator factory creates condition evaluators using the expression service\\n- writer/ (datasourcewriter.go, prom.go): Remote write support for recording rules and state metrics\\n- api/ (api_ruler.go, api_ruler_history.go): REST API endpoints for rule management and history querying\\n- provisioning/: Configuration as code support for rules, contact points, and policies\\n\\n**Execution Flow:**\\n1. ProvideService() initializes all components during startup\\n2. AlertNG.Run() starts the scheduler, state manager, multiorg alertmanager, and alerts router in separate goroutines\\n3. Scheduler.Run() periodically fetches rules from DBstore and evaluates them\\n4. Evaluations produce state transitions sent to the state manager\\n5. State manager persists states to InstanceDBStore and sends transitions to notifier\\n6. State transitions are recorded by the historian backend(s)\\n7. AlertsRouter sends notifications to external systems via the MultiOrgAlertmanager\\n8. Users query current state and history via the API endpoints\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1916,"cache_read_input_tokens":63936,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1916},"output_tokens":4,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"a2b79af9-a616-4a5b-b75e-110e6200be89","uuid":"a8870f77-9698-468c-8811-949f5fc1772e"}

Key components:\\n- NewScheduler() creates the scheduler with a RulesStore dependency\\n- alert_rule.go: Executes individual alert rules by querying data sources\\n- recording_rule.go: Executes Prometheus recording rules\\n- registry.go: Maintains a registry of all active rules and their evaluation state\\n- ticker/ticker.go: Manages evaluation intervals and timing\\n- retry.go: Implements backoff strategy for failed evaluations\\nThe scheduler fetches rules from DBstore.GetAlertRulesForScheduling() and evaluates them using the EvaluatorFactory.\\n\\n**3. State Manager (State Package)**\\nThe Manager (pkg/services/ngalert/state/manager.go) tracks the lifecycle of alert instances:\\n- manager.go: Core state tracking with NewManager() initialization\\n- state.go: State transition definitions (Normal, Alerting, Pending, NoData)\\n- cache.go: In-memory state cache for efficient lookups\\n- persist.go: StatePersister interface with three implementations:\\n  - persister_sync.go: Synchronous persistence\\n  - persister_async.go: Asynchronous periodic persistence\\n  - persister_sync_rule.go: Rule-aware state persistence\\n- multi_instance_reader.go: Handles state loading from database during startup\\nAfter the scheduler evaluates a rule, it sends state transitions to the state manager, which persists them to the instance database and forwards them to the notifier.\\n\\n**4. Notifier (Notifier Package)**\\nThe notification system manages alert routing to external systems:\\n- multiorg_alertmanager.go: MultiOrgAlertmanager orchestrates Alertmanager instances per organization\\n- alertmanager.go: Individual Alertmanager implementation wrapping the upstream Prometheus Alertmanager\\n- receiver_svc.go: ReceiverService manages contact point configurations\\n- silence_svc.go: SilenceService manages silences and mute timings\\n- alertmanager_config.go and config.go: Handle configuration persistence and validation\\n- alerts.go and silences.go: State management for alerts and silences\\nThe sender/router.go (AlertsRouter) sends state transitions from the state manager to the appropriate Alertmanager instance, which applies routing and grouping rules before sending to external notification channels.\\n\\n**5. History Writer (State/Historian Package)**\\nThe historian subsystem records alert state transitions for audit and querying:\\n- core.go: Core historian logic determining which transitions to record\\n- backend.go: Backend interface for pluggable storage\\n- Multiple backend implementations:\\n  - annotation.go: Stores state in Grafana annotations (AnnotationBackend)\\n  - loki.go: Remote Loki instance (RemoteLokiBackend)\\n  - prometheus.go: Prometheus remote write (RemotePrometheusBackend)\\n  - multiple.go: MultipleBackend for concurrent writes\\n- query.go: Queries historical state data\\n- model/rule.go: Historical rule models\\nThe state manager calls historian.Record() for each state transition, persisting them to the configured backend(s) for historical querying via the API.\\n\\n**Supporting Components:**\\n- eval/eval.go: Evaluator factory creates condition evaluators using the expression service\\n- writer/ (datasourcewriter.go, prom.go): Remote write support for recording rules and state metrics\\n- api/ (api_ruler.go, api_ruler_history.go): REST API endpoints for rule management and history querying\\n- provisioning/: Configuration as code support for rules, contact points, and policies\\n\\n**Execution Flow:**\\n1. ProvideService() initializes all components during startup\\n2. AlertNG.Run() starts the scheduler, state manager, multiorg alertmanager, and alerts router in separate goroutines\\n3. Scheduler.Run() periodically fetches rules from DBstore and evaluates them\\n4. Evaluations produce state transitions sent to the state manager\\n5. State manager persists states to InstanceDBStore and sends transitions to notifier\\n6. State transitions are recorded by the historian backend(s)\\n7.
